html body div h2: 
	
html body div h2: 
Abstract
html body div: 

html body div p: The Extensible Markup Language (XML) is a subset of SGML that is completely
described in this document. Its goal is to enable generic SGML to be served,
received, and processed on the Web in the way that is now possible with HTML.
XML has been designed for ease of implementation and for interoperability
with both SGML and HTML.
html body div: 

html body: 

html body div: 

html body div h2: 
	
html body div h2: 
Status of this Document
html body div: 

html body div p: 
	
html body div p em: This section describes the status of this document at the time of its publication.
			Other documents may supersede this document. A list of current W3C publications and the
			latest revision of this technical report can be found in the 
html body div p em a: W3C technical reports index
html body div p em:  at
			http://www.w3.org/TR/.
html body div p: 

html body div: 

html body div p: This document specifies a syntax created by subsetting an existing, widely
used international text processing standard (Standard Generalized Markup Language,
ISO 8879:1986(E) as amended and corrected) for use on the World Wide Web.
It is a product of the 
html body div p a: XML Core Working Group
html body div p: 
as part of the 
html body div p a: XML Activity
html body div p: .

html body div: 

html body div p: On 29 September 2006 this document was edited in place to remove a
number of spurious and potentially misleading spaces.
html body div: 

html body div p: The English version of this specification is the only normative version. However,
for translations of this document, see 
html body div p a: http://www.w3.org/2003/03/Translations/byTechnology?technology=xml11
html body div p: .

html body div: 

html body div p: This document is a 
html body div p a: W3C Recommendation
html body div p: .
			This second edition is 
html body div p em: not
html body div p:  a new version of XML. As a convenience to readers,
      it incorporates the changes dictated by the accumulated errata (available at
	
html body div p a: http://www.w3.org/XML/xml-V11-1e-errata
html body div p: ) to the 
html body div p a: First
      Edition of XML 1.1, dated 4 February 2004
html body div p: . In addition, the markup introduced to clarify when prescriptive 
      keywords are used
      in the formal sense defined in 
html body div p a: [IETF RFC 2119]
html body div p: , has been modified to better match the intent of 
html body div p a: [IETF RFC 2119]
html body div p: . 
			This edition supersedes the previous 
html body div p a: W3C Recommendation
			of 4 February 2004
html body div p: .

html body div: 

html body div p: Please report errors in this document to the public 
html body div p a: xml-editor@w3.org
html body div p:  mailing list; 
html body div p a: archives
html body div p:  are available. For the convenience of readers,
				an 
html body div p a: XHTML version with color-coded revision indicators
html body div p:  is
				also provided; this version highlights each change due to an erratum published in the
	
html body div p a: errata list
html body div p: , together with a link to the particular
				erratum in that list. Most of the errata in the list provide a rationale for the change.
				The errata list for this second edition is available at 
html body div p a: http://www.w3.org/XML/xml-V11-2e-errata
html body div p: .

html body div: 

html body div p: An implementation report is available at

html body div: 

html body div p: This document has been reviewed by W3C Members, by software developers, and by other W3C groups and interested parties, and is endorsed by the Director as a W3C Recommendation. It is a stable document and may be used as reference material or cited from another document. W3C's role in making the Recommendation is to draw attention to the specification and to promote its widespread deployment. This enhances the functionality and interoperability of the Web.

html body div div: 

html body div div h2: 

html body div div h2: 
1 Introduction
html body div div: 

html body div div p: Extensible Markup Language, abbreviated XML, describes a class of data
objects called 
html body div div p a: XML documents
html body div div p:  and partially
describes the behavior of computer programs which process them. XML is an
application profile or restricted form of SGML, the Standard Generalized Markup
Language 
html body div div p a: [ISO 8879]
html body div div p: . By construction, XML documents are conforming
SGML documents.
html body div div: 

html body div div p: XML documents are made up of storage units called 
html body div div p a: entities
html body div div p: ,
which contain either parsed or unparsed data. Parsed data is made up of 
html body div div p a: characters
html body div div p: , some of which form 
html body div div p a: character
data
html body div div p: , and some of which form 
html body div div p a: markup
html body div div p: .
Markup encodes a description of the document's storage layout and logical
structure. XML provides a mechanism to impose constraints on the storage layout
and logical structure.
html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : A software module called
an 
html body div div p b: XML processor
html body div div p:  is used to read XML documents and provide access
to their content and structure.]
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : It
is assumed that an XML processor is doing its work on behalf of another module,
called the 
html body div div p b: application
html body div div p: .] This specification describes
the required behavior of an XML processor in terms of how it must read XML
data and the information it must provide to the application.
html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h3: 

html body div div div h3: 
1.1 Origin and Goals
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: XML was developed by an XML Working Group (originally known as the SGML
Editorial Review Board) formed under the auspices of the World Wide Web Consortium
(W3C) in 1996. It was chaired by Jon Bosak of Sun Microsystems with the active
participation of an XML Special Interest Group (previously known as the SGML
Working Group) also organized by the W3C. The membership of the XML Working
Group is given in an appendix. Dan Connolly served as the Working Group's contact with
the W3C.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The design goals for XML are:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: XML shall be straightforwardly usable over the Internet.
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: XML shall support a wide variety of applications.
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: XML shall be compatible with SGML.
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: It shall be easy to write programs which process XML documents.
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: The number of optional features in XML is to be kept to the absolute
minimum, ideally zero.
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: XML documents should be human-legible and reasonably clear.
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: The XML design should be prepared quickly.
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: The design of XML shall be formal and concise.
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: XML documents shall be easy to create.
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: Terseness in XML markup is of minimal importance.
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: This specification, together with associated standards (Unicode

html body div div div p a: [Unicode]
html body div div div p:  and ISO/IEC 10646 
html body div div div p a: [ISO/IEC 10646]
html body div div div p: 
for characters, Internet RFC 3066 
html body div div div p a: [IETF RFC 3066]
html body div div div p:  for
language identification tags, ISO 639 
html body div div div p a: [ISO 639]
html body div div div p: 
for language name codes, and ISO 3166 
html body div div div p a: [ISO 3166]
html body div div div p:  for
country name codes), provides all the information necessary to
understand XML Version 1.1 and construct computer
programs to process it.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: This version of the XML specification may be distributed freely, as long as
all text and legal notices remain intact.
html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h3: 

html body div div div h3: 
1.2 Terminology
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The terminology used to describe XML documents is defined in the body of
this specification. The key words 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p em: MUST NOT
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p em: REQUIRED
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p em: SHALL
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p em: SHALL NOT
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p em: SHOULD NOT
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p em: RECOMMENDED
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p em: MAY
html body div div div p: , and 
html body div div div p em: OPTIONAL
html body div div div p: , when 
html body div div div p em: EMPHASIZED
html body div div div p: , are to be interpreted as described in 
html body div div div p a: [IETF RFC 2119]
html body div div div p: . In addition, the terms defined in the following list are used in building
those definitions and in describing the actions of an XML processor:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dt: error
html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dd: 

html body div div div dl dd p: 
									[
html body div div div dl dd p a: Definition
html body div div div dl dd p: : A violation of the rules of this specification;
results are undefined. Unless otherwise specified, failure to observe a prescription of this specification indicated by one of the keywords 
html body div div div dl dd p em: MUST
html body div div div dl dd p: ,
html body div div div dl dd p em: REQUIRED
html body div div div dl dd p: ,
html body div div div dl dd p em: MUST NOT
html body div div div dl dd p: ,
html body div div div dl dd p em: SHALL
html body div div div dl dd p:  and 
html body div div div dl dd p em: SHALL NOT
html body div div div dl dd p:  is an error.  Conforming software 
html body div div div dl dd p em: MAY
html body div div div dl dd p:  detect and report an error
and 
html body div div div dl dd p em: MAY
html body div div div dl dd p:  recover from it.]

html body div div div dl dd: 

html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dt: fatal error
html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dd: 

html body div div div dl dd p: 
									[
html body div div div dl dd p a: Definition
html body div div div dl dd p: : An error which a conforming 
html body div div div dl dd p a: XML processor
html body div div div dl dd p: 

html body div div div dl dd p em: MUST
html body div div div dl dd p:  detect and report to the application.
After encountering a fatal error, the processor 
html body div div div dl dd p em: MAY
html body div div div dl dd p:  continue processing the
data to search for further errors and 
html body div div div dl dd p em: MAY
html body div div div dl dd p:  report such errors to the application.
In order to support correction of errors, the processor 
html body div div div dl dd p em: MAY
html body div div div dl dd p:  make unprocessed
data from the document (with intermingled character data and markup) available

html body div div div dl dd p em: MUST NOT

html body div div div dl dd p em: MUST NOT
html body div div div dl dd p:  continue to pass character

in the normal way).]

1.3 Rationale and list of changes for XML 1.1
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The W3C's XML 1.0 Recommendation was first issued in 1998, and
despite the issuance of many errata culminating in a Third Edition
of 2004, has remained (by intention) unchanged with respect to what
is well-formed XML and what is not. This stability has been
extremely useful for interoperability. However, the Unicode
Standard on which XML 1.0 relies for character specifications has
not remained static, evolving from version 2.0 to version 4.0 and
beyond. Characters not present in Unicode 2.0 may already be used
in XML 1.0 character data. However, they are not allowed in XML
names such as element type names, attribute names, enumerated
attribute values, processing instruction targets, and so on. In
addition, some characters that should have been permitted in XML
names were not, due to oversights and inconsistencies in Unicode
2.0.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The overall philosophy of names has changed since XML 1.0.
Whereas XML 1.0 provided a rigid definition of names, wherein
everything that was not permitted was forbidden, XML 1.1 names are
designed so that everything that is not forbidden (for a specific
reason) is permitted. Since Unicode will continue to grow past
version 4.0, further changes to XML can be avoided by allowing
almost any character, including those not yet assigned, in
names.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: In addition, XML 1.0 attempts to adapt to the line-end
conventions of various modern operating systems, but discriminates
against the conventions used on IBM and IBM-compatible mainframes.
As a result, XML documents on mainframes are not plain text files
according to the local conventions. XML 1.0 documents generated on
mainframes must either violate the local line-end conventions, or
employ otherwise unnecessary translation phases before parsing and
after generation. Allowing straightforward interoperability is
particularly important when data stores are shared between
mainframe and non-mainframe systems (as opposed to being copied
from one to the other). Therefore XML 1.1 adds NEL (#x85) to the
list of line-end characters. For completeness, the Unicode line
separator character, #x2028, is also supported.

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Finally, there is considerable demand to define a standard representation
of arbitrary Unicode characters in XML documents. Therefore, XML 1.1
allows the use of character references to the control characters #x1 through
#x1F, most of which are forbidden in XML 1.0. For reasons of robustness,
however, these characters still cannot be used directly in documents. In
order to improve the robustness of character encoding detection, the additional
control characters #x7F through #x9F, which were freely allowed in XML 1.0
documents, now must also appear only as character references. (Whitespace
characters are of course exempt.) The minor sacrifice of backward compatibility
is considered not significant. Due to potential problems with APIs,
#x0 is still forbidden both directly and as a character reference.

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Finally, XML 1.1 defines a set of constraints called "full
normalization" on XML documents, which document creators

html body div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div p:  adhere to, and document processors

html body div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div p:  verify.  Using fully normalized documents
ensures that identity comparisons of names, attribute values, and
character content can be made correctly by simple binary comparison of
Unicode strings.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: A new XML version, rather than a set of errata to XML 1.0, is
being created because the changes affect the definition of
well-formed documents. XML 1.0 processors must continue to reject
documents that contain new characters in XML names, new line-end
conventions, and references to control characters. The distinction between XML 1.0 and XML 1.1 documents
is indicated by the version number information in the XML
declaration at the start of each document.

html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div h2:

2.3 Common Syntactic Constructs
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: This section defines some symbols used widely in the grammar.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p a: S
html body div div div p:  (white space) consists of one or more space (#x20)
characters, carriage returns, line feeds, or tabs.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div h5: 

html body div div div h5: 
White Space
html body div div div: 

html body div div div table: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 
[3]   
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: S
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td:  ::=   
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: (#x20 | #x9 | #xD | #xA)+
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p b: Note:
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: The presence of #xD in the above production is
maintained purely for backward compatibility with the

html body div div div div p a: First Edition
html body div div div div p: .
As explained in 
html body div div div div p a: 

html body div div div div p a b: 2.11 End-of-Line Handling
html body div div div div p a: 

html body div div div div p: ,
all #xD characters literally present in an XML document
are either removed or replaced by #xA characters before
any other processing is done. The only way to get a #xD character to match this production is to
use a character reference in an entity value literal.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: 
					[
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : A 
html body div div div p b: Name
html body div div div p:  is a token beginning
with a letter or one of a few punctuation characters, and continuing with
letters, digits, hyphens, underscores, colons, or full stops, together known
as name characters.] Names beginning with the string "
html body div div div p code: xml
html body div div div p: ",
or with any string which would match 
html body div div div p code: (('X'|'x') ('M'|'m') ('L'|'l'))
html body div div div p: ,
are reserved for standardization in this or future versions of this specification.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p b: Note:
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: The
Namespaces in XML Recommendation 
html body div div div div p a: [XML Names]
html body div div div div p:  assigns a meaning
to names containing colon characters. Therefore, authors should not use the
colon in XML names except for namespace purposes, but XML processors must
accept the colon as a name character.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: An 
html body div div div p a: Nmtoken
html body div div div p:  (name token) is any mixture of name
characters.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The first character of a Name 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be a NameStartChar, and any
other characters 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be NameChars; this mechanism is used to
prevent names from beginning with European (ASCII) digits or with
basic combining characters. Almost all characters are permitted in
names, except those which either are or reasonably could be used as
delimiters. The intention is to be inclusive rather than exclusive,
so that writing systems not yet encoded in Unicode can be used in
XML names. See 
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p a b: I Suggestions for XML Names
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p:  for suggestions on the creation of
names.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Document authors are encouraged to use names which are
meaningful words or combinations of words in natural languages, and
to avoid symbolic or white space characters in names. Note that
COLON, HYPHEN-MINUS, FULL STOP (period), LOW LINE (underscore), and
MIDDLE DOT are explicitly permitted.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The ASCII symbols and punctuation marks, along with a fairly
large group of Unicode symbol characters, are excluded from names
because they are more useful as delimiters in contexts where XML
names are used outside XML documents; providing this group gives
those contexts hard guarantees about what 
html body div div div p em: cannot
html body div div div p:  be part of
an XML name. The character #x037E, GREEK QUESTION MARK, is excluded
because when normalized it becomes a semicolon, which could change

2.4 Character Data and Markup
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p a: Text
html body div div div p:  consists of intermingled 
html body div div div p a: character data
html body div div div p:  and markup. [
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : 

html body div div div p b: Markup
html body div div div p:  takes the form of 
html body div div div p a: start-tags
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p a: end-tags
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p a: empty-element tags
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p a: entity references
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p a: character
references
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p a: comments
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p a: CDATA section
html body div div div p:  delimiters, 
html body div div div p a: document
type declarations
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p a: processing instructions
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p a: XML declarations
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p a: text declarations
html body div div div p: ,
and any white space that is at the top level of the document entity (that
is, outside the document element and not inside any other markup).]

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: 
					[
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : All text that is not markup
constitutes the 
html body div div div p b: character data
html body div div div p:  of the document.]

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The ampersand character (&) and the left angle bracket (<) 
html body div div div p em: MUST NOT
html body div div div p:  appear
in their literal form, except when used as markup delimiters, or
within a 
html body div div div p a: comment
html body div div div p: , a 
html body div div div p a: processing
instruction
html body div div div p: , or a 
html body div div div p a: CDATA section
html body div div div p: .

If they are needed elsewhere, they 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be 
html body div div div p a: escaped
html body div div div p: 
using either 
html body div div div p a: numeric character references
html body div div div p: 
or the strings "
html body div div div p code: &amp;
html body div div div p: " and "
html body div div div p code: &lt;
html body div div div p: "
respectively. The right angle bracket (>) 
html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  be represented using the string "
html body div div div p code: &gt;
html body div div div p: ",
and 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p a: for compatibility
html body div div div p: , be escaped
using either "
html body div div div p code: &gt;
html body div div div p: " or a character reference when it
appears in the string "
html body div div div p code: ]]>
html body div div div p: " in content, when
that string is not marking the end of a 
html body div div div p a: CDATA
section
html body div div div p: .

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: In the content of elements, character data is any string of characters
which does not contain the start-delimiter of any markup or the
CDATA-section-close delimiter,
"
html body div div div p code: ]]>
html body div div div p: ".
In a CDATA section,
character data is any string of characters not including the CDATA-section-close
delimiter.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: To allow attribute values to contain both single and double quotes, the
apostrophe or single-quote character (') 
html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  be represented as "
html body div div div p code: &apos;
html body div div div p: ",
and the double-quote character (") as "
html body div div div p code: &quot;
html body div div div p: ".

html body div div div:

html body div div div p: ; an XML processor

2.7 CDATA Sections
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: 
					[
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : 

html body div div div p b: CDATA sections
html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  occur anywhere character data may occur; they are used to escape blocks
of text containing characters which would otherwise be recognized as markup.
CDATA sections begin with the string "
html body div div div p code: <![CDATA[
html body div div div p: "
and end with the string "
html body div div div p code: ]]>
html body div div div p: ":]

html body div div div p: Note

html body div div div p a: doctypedecl
html body div div div p:

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The markup declarations 
html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  be made up in whole or in part of the 
html body div div div p a: replacement text
html body div div div p:  of 
html body div div div p a: parameter
entities
html body div div div p: . The productions later in this specification for individual
nonterminals (
html body div div div p a: elementdecl
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p a: AttlistDecl
html body div div div p: ,
and so on) describe the declarations 
html body div div div p em: after
html body div div div p:  all the parameter
entities have been 
html body div div div p a: included
html body div div div p: .

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Parameter
entity references are recognized anywhere in the DTD (internal and external
subsets and external parameter entities), except in literals, processing instructions,
comments, and the contents of ignored conditional sections (see 
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p a b: 3.4 Conditional Sections
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p: ).
They are also recognized in entity value literals. The use of parameter entities
in the internal subset is restricted as described below.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p b: Validity constraint: Root Element Type
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: The 
html body div div div div p a: Name
html body div div div div p: 
in the document type declaration 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  match the element type of the 
html body div div div div p a: root element
html body div div div div p: .

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p b: Validity constraint: Proper Declaration/PE Nesting
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Parameter-entity 
html body div div div div p a: replacement text
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  be properly nested with markup declarations. That is to say, if either
the first character or the last character of a markup declaration (
html body div div div div p a: markupdecl
html body div div div div p: 
above) is contained in the replacement text for a 
html body div div div div p a: parameter-entity
reference
html body div div div div p: , both 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  be contained in the same replacement text.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p b: Well-formedness constraint: PEs in Internal Subset
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: In
the internal DTD subset, 
html body div div div div p a: parameter-entity references
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p em: MUST NOT
html body div div div div p:  occur within markup declarations; they 
html body div div div div p span: may
html body div div div div p:  occur where markup declarations can occur.
(This does not apply to references that occur in external parameter entities
or to the external subset.)
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p b: Well-formedness constraint: External Subset
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: The external subset, if any, 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  match the production for 
html body div div div div p a: extSubset
html body div div div div p: .

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p b: Well-formedness constraint: PE Between Declarations
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: The replacement text of a parameter entity reference
in a 
html body div div div div p a: DeclSep
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  match the production 
html body div div div div p a: extSubsetDecl
html body div div div div p: .

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Like the internal subset, the external subset and any external parameter
entities referenced
in a 
html body div div div p a: DeclSep
html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  consist of a series of
complete markup declarations of the types allowed by the non-terminal symbol 
html body div div div p a: markupdecl
html body div div div p: , interspersed with white space or 
html body div div div p a: parameter-entity references
html body div div div p: . However, portions of
the contents of the external subset or of these
external parameter entities 
html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  conditionally be ignored by using the 
html body div div div p a: conditional section
html body div div div p:  construct; this is not
allowed in the internal subset but is
allowed in external parameter entities referenced in the internal subset.

html body div div div p: The external subset and external parameter entities also differ from the
internal subset in that in them, 
html body div div div p a: parameter-entity
references
html body div div div p:  are permitted 
html body div div div p em: within
html body div div div p:  markup declarations,
not only 
html body div div div p em: between
html body div div div p:  markup declarations.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: An example of an XML document with a document type declaration:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div pre: <?xml version="1.1"?>
<!DOCTYPE greeting SYSTEM "hello.dtd">
<greeting>Hello, world!</greeting> 
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The 
html body div div div p a: system identifier
html body div div div p: 
					"
html body div div div p code: hello.dtd
html body div div div p: "
gives the address (a URI reference) of a DTD for the document.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The declarations can also be given locally, as in this example:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div pre: <?xml version="1.1" encoding="UTF-8" ?>
<!DOCTYPE greeting [
<!ELEMENT greeting (#PCDATA)>
]>
<greeting>Hello, world!</greeting>
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: If both the external and internal subsets are used, the internal subset

html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be considered to occur before the external subset. 
This has the effect that entity and attribute-list declarations in the internal
subset take precedence over those in the external subset.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: 
					If a document is well-formed or valid XML 1.0, and provided it
does not contain any control characters
in the range [#x7F-#x9F] other than as character escapes, it may be
made well-formed or valid XML 1.1 respectively simply by changing the
version number.

2.9 Standalone Document Declaration
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Markup declarations can affect the content of the document, as passed from
an 
html body div div div p a: XML processor
html body div div div p:  to an application; examples
are attribute defaults and entity declarations. The standalone document declaration,
which 
html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  appear as a component of the XML declaration, signals whether or
not there are such declarations which appear external to the 
html body div div div p a: document
entity
html body div div div p: 
or in parameter entities. [
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : An 
html body div div div p b: external
markup declaration
html body div div div p:  is defined as a markup declaration occurring in
the external subset or in a parameter entity (external or internal, the latter
being included because non-validating processors are not required to read
them).]

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h5: 

html body div div div h5:

html body div div div:

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: SDDecl
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td:  ::=   
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code span: 


html body div div div table tbody tr td code span a: S
html body div div div table tbody tr td code span: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code:  'standalone' 
html body div div div table tbody tr td code a: Eq
html body div div div table tbody tr td code: 
(("'" ('yes' | 'no') "'") | ('"' ('yes' | 'no') '"'))

html body div div div p: In a standalone document declaration, the value "yes" indicates
that there are no 
html body div div div p a: external markup declarations
html body div div div p:  which
affect the information passed from the XML processor to the application. The
value "no" indicates that there are or may be such external
markup declarations. Note that the standalone document declaration only denotes
the presence of external 
html body div div div p em: declarations
html body div div div p: ; the presence, in a document,
of references to external 
html body div div div p em: entities
html body div div div p: , when those entities are internally
declared, does not change its standalone status.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: If there are no external markup declarations, the standalone document declaration
has no meaning. If there are external markup declarations but there is no
standalone document declaration, the value "no" is assumed.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Any XML document for which 
html body div div div p code: standalone="no"
html body div div div p:  holds can be converted
algorithmically to a standalone document, which may be desirable for some
network delivery applications.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p b: Validity constraint: Standalone Document Declaration
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: The
standalone document declaration 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  have the value "no" if
any external markup declarations contain declarations of:
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div ul li p: attributes with 
html body div div div div ul li p a: default
html body div div div div ul li p:  values,
if elements to which these attributes apply appear in the document without
specifications of values for these attributes, or
html body div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div ul li p: entities (other than 
html body div div div div ul li p code: amp
html body div div div div ul li p: ,

html body div div div div ul li p code: lt
html body div div div div ul li p: ,

html body div div div div ul li p code: gt
html body div div div div ul li p: ,

html body div div div div ul li p code: apos
html body div div div div ul li p: ,

html body div div div div ul li p code: quot
html body div div div div ul li p: ), if 
html body div div div div ul li p a: references
html body div div div div ul li p: 
to those entities appear in the document, or
html body div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div ul li p: attributes with
tokenized types, where the
attribute appears in the document with a value such that

html body div div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div div ul li p a cite: normalization
html body div div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div div ul li p: 
will produce a different value from that which would be produced
in the absence of the declaration, or
html body div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div ul li p: element types with 
html body div div div div ul li p a: element content
html body div div div div ul li p: ,
if white space occurs directly within any instance of those types.

2.10 White Space Handling
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: In editing XML documents, it is often convenient to use "white space"
(spaces, tabs, and blank lines)
to set apart the markup for greater readability. Such white space is typically
not intended for inclusion in the delivered version of the document. On the
other hand, "significant" white space that should be preserved
in the delivered version is common, for example in poetry and source code.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: An 
html body div div div p a: XML processor
html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  always pass
all characters in a document that are not markup through to the application.
A 
html body div div div p a:  validating XML processor
html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  also
inform the application which of these characters constitute white space appearing
in 
html body div div div p a: element content
html body div div div p: .

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: A special 
html body div div div p a: attribute
html body div div div p:  named 
html body div div div p code: xml:space
html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  be attached to an element to signal an intention that in that element,
white space should be preserved by applications. In valid documents, this
attribute, like any other, 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be 
html body div div div p a: declared
html body div div div p: 
if it is used. When declared, it 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be given as an 
html body div div div p a: enumerated
type
html body div div div p:  whose values
are one or both of "default" and "preserve".
For example:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div pre: <!ATTLIST poem  xml:space (default|preserve) 'preserve'>
<!ATTLIST pre xml:space (preserve) #FIXED 'preserve'>
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The value "default" signals that applications' default white-space
processing modes are acceptable for this element; the value "preserve"
indicates the intent that applications preserve all the white space. This
declared intent is considered to apply to all elements within the content
of the element where it is specified, unless overridden with
another instance of the 
html body div div div p code: xml:space
html body div div div p:  attribute. This specification does not give meaning to any value of 
html body div div div p code: xml:space
html body div div div p:  other than "default" and "preserve". It is an error for other values to be specified; the XML processor 
html body div div div p em: MAY
html body div div div p:  report the error or 
html body div div div p em: MAY
html body div div div p:  recover by ignoring the attribute specification or by reporting the (erroneous) value to the application. Applications may ignore or reject erroneous values.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The 
html body div div div p a: root element
html body div div div p:  of any document is considered
to have signaled no intentions as regards application space handling, unless
it provides a value for this attribute or the attribute is declared with a
default value.
html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h3: 

html body div div div h3: 
2.11 End-of-Line Handling
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: XML 
html body div div div p a: parsed entities
html body div div div p:  are often stored
in computer files which, for editing convenience, are organized into lines.
These lines are typically separated by some combination of the characters
CARRIAGE RETURN (#xD) and LINE FEED (#xA).
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: To
simplify the tasks of 
html body div div div p a: applications
html body div div div p: , the

html body div div div p a: XML
processor
html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  behave as if it normalized all line breaks in external parsed
entities (including the document entity) on input, before parsing, by translating
all of the following to a single #xA character:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: the two-character sequence #xD #xA
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: the two-character sequence #xD #x85
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: the single character #x85
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: the single character #x2028
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: any #xD character that is not immediately followed by #xA or #x85.
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p:   The characters #x85 and #x2028 cannot be reliably recognized and
translated until an entity's encoding declaration (if present) has
been read.  Therefore, it is a fatal error to use them within the XML
declaration or text declaration.

html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h3: 

html body div div div h3: 
2.12 Language Identification
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: In document processing, it is often useful to identify the natural or formal
language in which the content is written. A special 
html body div div div p a: attribute
html body div div div p: 
named 
html body div div div p code: xml:lang
html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  be inserted in documents to specify the language
used in the contents and attribute values of any element in an XML document.
In valid documents, this attribute, like any other, 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be 
html body div div div p a: declared
html body div div div p: 
if it is used. The
values of the attribute are language identifiers as defined by 
html body div div div p a: [IETF RFC 3066]
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p cite: Tags
for the Identification of Languages
html body div div div p: , or its successor; in addition, the empty string 
html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  be specified.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: (Productions 33 through 38 have been removed.)
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: For example:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div pre: <p xml:lang="en">The quick brown fox jumps over the lazy dog.</p>
<p xml:lang="en-GB">What colour is it?</p>
<p xml:lang="en-US">What color is it?</p>
<sp who="Faust" desc='leise' xml:lang="de">
<l>Habe nun, ach! Philosophie,</l>
<l>Juristerei, und Medizin</l>
<l>und leider auch Theologie</l>
<l>durchaus studiert mit hei&#xDF;em Bem&#xFC;h'n.</l>
</sp>
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The 
html body div div div p span: 
						language specified by
html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p code: xml:lang
html body div div div p: 


html body div div div p span: 
						applies
html body div div div p: 
     to  the element where it is specified
html body div div div p span: 
						
         (including the values of its attributes), and  to all elements in its content
html body div div div p:  unless
     overridden with 
html body div div div p span: 
						another
html body div div div p:  instance of 
html body div div div p code: xml:lang
html body div div div p: . In particular, the empty value of 
html body div div div p code: xml:lang
html body div div div p:  is used on an element B to override
         a specification of 
html body div div div p code: xml:lang
html body div div div p:  on an enclosing element A, without specifying another language. Within B,
         it is considered that there is no language information available, just as if 
html body div div div p code: xml:lang
html body div div div p:  had not been specified
         on B or any of its ancestors.
html body div div div p span: 
						 Applications determine which of an element's attribute values
     and which parts of its character content, if any, are treated as language-dependent values described by 
html body div div div p span code: xml:lang
html body div div div p span: .

html body div div div p: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p b: Note:
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Language information may also be provided by external transport protocols (e.g. HTTP or
MIME). When available, this information may be used by XML applications, but the more local
information provided by 
html body div div div div p code: xml:lang
html body div div div div p:  should be considered to override it.

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: A simple declaration for 
html body div div div p code: xml:lang
html body div div div p:  might take the form
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div pre: xml:lang CDATA #IMPLIED
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: but specific default values 
html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  also be given, if appropriate. In a collection
of French poems for English students, with glosses and notes in English, the 
html body div div div p code: xml:lang
html body div div div p: 
attribute might be declared this way:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div pre: <!ATTLIST poem   xml:lang CDATA 'fr'>
<!ATTLIST gloss  xml:lang CDATA 'en'>
<!ATTLIST note   xml:lang CDATA 'en'>
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h3: 

html body div div div h3: 
2.13 Normalization Checking
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: All XML 
html body div div div p a:  parsed
entities
html body div div div p:  (including 
html body div div div p a:  document
entities
html body div div div p: )
html body div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div p:  be 
html body div div div p a: fully
normalized
html body div div div p:  as per the definition of

html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p a b: B Definitions for Character Normalization
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p:  supplemented by the following definitions of

html body div div div p em: 

html body div div div p em: 
relevant constructs
html body div div div p:  for XML:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: The 
html body div div div ol li p a: 
replacement text
html body div div div ol li p:  of all 
html body div div div ol li p a: parsed
entities
html body div div div ol li p: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li p: All text matching, in context, one of the following
productions:
html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol li ol: 

html body div div div ol li ol li: 

html body div div div ol li ol li p: 

html body div div div ol li ol li p a: 
CData
html body div div div ol li ol li p: 

html body div div div ol li ol li: 

html body div div div ol li ol: 

html body div div div ol li ol li: 

html body div div div ol li ol li p: 

html body div div div ol li ol li p a: 
CharData
html body div div div ol li ol li p: 

html body div div div ol li ol li: 

html body div div div ol li ol: 

html body div div div ol li ol li: 

html body div div div ol li ol li p: 

html body div div div ol li ol li p a: 
content
html body div div div ol li ol li p: 

html body div div div ol li ol li: 

html body div div div ol li ol: 

html body div div div ol li ol li: 

html body div div div ol li ol li p: 

html body div div div ol li ol li p a:  Name
html body div div div ol li ol li p: 

html body div div div ol li ol li: 

html body div div div ol li ol: 

html body div div div ol li ol li: 

html body div div div ol li ol li p: 

html body div div div ol li ol li p a: 
Nmtoken
html body div div div ol li ol li p: 

html body div div div ol li ol li: 

html body div div div ol li ol: 

html body div div div ol li: 

html body div div div ol: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: However, a document is still well-formed even if it is not

html body div div div p a: fully normalized
html body div div div p: .
XML processors 
html body div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div p:  provide a user option to verify that the document being
processed is in 
html body div div div p a: fully normalized
html body div div div p:  form, and report to the application whether
it is or not. The option to not verify 
html body div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div p:  be chosen only when the
input text is 
html body div div div p a: certified
html body div div div p: ,
as defined by 
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p a b: B Definitions for Character Normalization
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p: .

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The verification of full normalization 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be carried out as if by
first verifying that the entity is in 
html body div div div p a: include-normalized
html body div div div p: 
form as defined by 
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p a b: B Definitions for Character Normalization
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p:  and by then verifying that none of the relevant
constructs listed above begins (after character references are
expanded) with a 
html body div div div p a: composing character
html body div div div p:  as defined by

html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p a b: B Definitions for Character Normalization
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p: .
Non-validating processors 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  ignore possible
denormalizations that would be caused by inclusion of external
entities that they do not read.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p b: Note:
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: The 
html body div div div div p a: composing character
html body div div div div p:  are all
Unicode characters of non-zero combining class, plus a small number
of class-zero characters that nevertheless take part as a
non-initial character in certain Unicode canonical
decompositions.  Since these characters are meant to follow
base characters, restricting relevant constructs (including
content) from beginning with a 
html body div div div div p a: composing character
html body div div div div p:  does not
meaningfully diminish the expressiveness of XML.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: If, while verifying full normalization, a processor encounters
characters for which it cannot determine the normalization
properties (i.e., characters introduced in a version of Unicode 
html body div div div p a: [Unicode]
html body div div div p: 
later than the one used in the implementation of the processor),
then the processor 
html body div div div p em: MAY
html body div div div p: , at user option, ignore any possible
denormalizations caused by these characters. The option to ignore
those denormalizations 
html body div div div p em: SHOULD NOT
html body div div div p:  be chosen by applications when
reliability or security are critical.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p:  XML processors 
html body div div div p em: MUST NOT
html body div div div p:  transform the input to be in

html body div div div p a: fully normalized
html body div div div p:  form.
XML applications that create XML 1.1 output
from either XML 1.1 or XML 1.0 input 
html body div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div p:  ensure that the output
is 
html body div div div p a: fully normalized
html body div div div p: ; it is not necessary for internal processing
forms to be 
html body div div div p a: fully normalized
html body div div div p: .

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The purpose of this section is to strongly encourage XML
processors to ensure that the creators of XML documents have
properly normalized them, so that XML applications can make tests
such as identity comparisons of strings without having to worry
about the different possible "spellings" of strings which
Unicode allows.

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: When entities are in a non-Unicode encoding, if the processor
transcodes them to Unicode, it 
html body div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div p:  use a normalizing transcoder.

html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div h2: 

html body div div h2: 
3 Logical Structures
html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : Each 
html body div div p a: XML
document

The optional character following a name or list governs whether the element
or the content particles in the list may occur one or more (
html body div div div div p code: +
html body div div div div p: ),
zero or more (
html body div div div div p code: *
html body div div div div p: ), or zero or one times (
html body div div div div p code: ?
html body div div div div p: ). The
absence of such an operator means that the element or content particle 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p: 
appear exactly once. This syntax and meaning are identical to those used in
the productions in this specification.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: The content of an element matches a content model if and only if it is
possible to trace out a path through the content model, obeying the sequence,
choice, and repetition operators and matching each element in the content
against an element type in the content model. 
html body div div div div p a: For
compatibility
html body div div div div p: , it is an error if the content model
allows an element to match more than one occurrence of an element type in the
content model. For more information, see

html body div div div div p b: #FIXED

html body div div div div p em: MUST

value declaration, it

specified for all elements of the type in the attribute-list declaration.

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div div p: 

html body div div div div div p: 

html body div div div div div p b: Validity constraint: Attribute Default Value Syntactically Correct
html body div div div div div p: 

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div div p: The declared default value 
html body div div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div div p:  meet the syntactic
constraints of the declared attribute type.
html body div div div div div p span: 
								 That is, the default value of an attribute:
html body div div div div div p: 

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div div ul li p: 
									of type IDREF or ENTITY must match the 
html body div div div div div ul li p a: Name
html body div div div div div ul li p:  production;
html body div div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div div ul li p: 
									of type IDREFS or ENTITIES must match the 
html body div div div div div ul li p a: Names
html body div div div div div ul li p:  production;
html body div div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div div ul li p: 
									of type NMTOKEN must match the 
html body div div div div div ul li p a: Nmtoken
html body div div div div div ul li p:  production;
html body div div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div div ul li p: 
									of type NMTOKENS must match the 
html body div div div div div ul li p a: Nmtokens
html body div div div div div ul li p:  production;
html body div div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div div ul li p: 
									of an 
html body div div div div div ul li p a: enumerated type
html body div div div div div ul li p:  (either a 
html body div div div div div ul li p a: NOTATION
html body div div div div div ul li p:  type or an 
html body div div div div div ul li p a: enumeration
html body div div div div div ul li p: ) must match one of the enumerated values.
html body div div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div div p: Note that only the
syntactic constraints of the type are required here; other constraints (e.g.
that the value be the name of a declared unparsed entity, for an attribute of
type ENTITY) 

html body div div div div div p span: 
								will be reported by a validating
parser only if an element without a specification for this attribute
actually occurs
html body div div div div div p: .

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div div p: 

html body div div div div div p: 

html body div div div div div p b: Validity constraint: Fixed Attribute Default
html body div div div div div p: 

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div div p: If an attribute
has a default value declared with the 
html body div div div div div p b: #FIXED
html body div div div div div p:  keyword, instances of
that attribute 
html body div div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div div p:  match the default value.
html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Examples of attribute-list declarations:
html body div div div div:

name    CDATA   #IMPLIED>
<!ATTLIST list
type    (bullets|ordered|glossary)  "ordered">
<!ATTLIST form

3.3.3 Attribute-Value Normalization
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Before the value of an attribute is passed to the application or checked
for validity, the XML processor 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  normalize the attribute value by applying
the algorithm below, or by using some other method such that the value passed
to the application is the same as that produced by the algorithm.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div ol: 

html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol li p: All line breaks 
html body div div div div ol li p em: MUST
html body div div div div ol li p:  have been normalized on input to #xA as described
in 
html body div div div div ol li p a: 

html body div div div div ol li p a b: 2.11 End-of-Line Handling
html body div div div div ol li p a: 

html body div div div div ol li p: , so the rest of this algorithm operates
on text normalized in this way.
html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol: 

html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol li p: Begin with a normalized value consisting of the empty string.
html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol: 

html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol li p: For each character, entity reference, or character reference in the
unnormalized attribute value, beginning with the first and continuing to the
last, do the following:
html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol li ul: 

html body div div div div ol li ul li: 

html body div div div div ol li ul li p: For a character reference, append the referenced character to the
normalized value.
html body div div div div ol li ul li: 

html body div div div div ol li ul: 

html body div div div div ol li ul li: 

html body div div div div ol li ul li p: For an entity reference, recursively apply step 3 of this algorithm
to the replacement text of the entity.
html body div div div div ol li ul li: 

html body div div div div ol li ul: 

html body div div div div ol li ul li: 

html body div div div div ol li ul li p: For a white space character (#x20, #xD, #xA, #x9), append a space
character (#x20) to the normalized value.
html body div div div div ol li ul li: 

html body div div div div ol li ul: 

html body div div div div ol li ul li: 

html body div div div div ol li ul li p: For another character, append the character to the normalized value.
html body div div div div ol li ul li: 

html body div div div div ol li ul: 

html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: If the attribute type is not CDATA, then the XML processor 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  further
process the normalized attribute value by discarding any leading and trailing
space (#x20) characters, and by replacing sequences of space (#x20) characters
by a single space (#x20) character.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Note that if the unnormalized attribute value contains a character reference
to a white space character other than space (#x20), the normalized value contains
the referenced character itself (#xD, #xA or #x9). This contrasts with the
case where the unnormalized value contains a white space character (not a
reference), which is replaced with a space character (#x20) in the normalized
value and also contrasts with the case where the unnormalized value contains
an entity reference whose replacement text contains a white space character;
being recursively processed, the white space character is replaced with a
space character (#x20) in the normalized value.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: All attributes for which no declaration has been read 
html body div div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div div p:  be treated
by a non-validating processor as if declared 
html body div div div div p b: CDATA
html body div div div div p: .

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: It
is an error if an

html body div div div div p a: attribute
value
html body div div div div p:  contains a 
html body div div div div p a: reference
html body div div div div p:  to an
entity for which no declaration has been read.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Following are examples of attribute normalization. Given the following
declarations:
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div div pre: <!ENTITY d "&#xD;">
<!ENTITY a "&#xA;">
<!ENTITY da "&#xD;&#xA;">
html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: the attribute specifications in the left column below would be normalized
to the character sequences of the middle column if the attribute 
html body div div div div p code: a
html body div div div div p: 
is declared 
html body div div div div p b: NMTOKENS
html body div div div div p:  and to those of the right columns if 
html body div div div div p code: a
html body div div div div p: 
is declared 
html body div div div div p b: CDATA
html body div div div div p: .

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div table:

html body div div div div table thead tr: 

html body div div div div table thead tr th: a is NMTOKENS
html body div div div div table thead tr:

html body div div div div table thead tr:

html body div div div div table tbody tr td div:

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p b: Validity constraint: Proper Conditional Section/PE Nesting
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: If any of the "
html body div div div div p code: <![
html body div div div div p: ",
"
html body div div div div p code: [
html body div div div div p: ", or "
html body div div div div p code: ]]>
html body div div div div p: " of a conditional section is contained
in the replacement text for a parameter-entity reference, all of them 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p: 
be contained in the same replacement text.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Like the internal and external DTD subsets, a conditional section may contain
one or more complete declarations, comments, processing instructions, or nested
conditional sections, intermingled with white space.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: If the keyword of the conditional section is 
html body div div div p b: INCLUDE
html body div div div p: , then the
contents of the conditional section 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be 

html body div div div p span: processed as
html body div div div p: 
part of the DTD. If the keyword of
the conditional section is 
html body div div div p b: IGNORE
html body div div div p: , then the contents of the conditional
section 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p: 


html body div div div p span: 

html body div div div p span em: NOT
html body div div div p span:  be processed as
html body div div div p:  part of the DTD.
If a conditional section with a keyword of 
html body div div div p b: INCLUDE
html body div div div p:  occurs within
a larger conditional section with a keyword of 
html body div div div p b: IGNORE
html body div div div p: , both the outer
and the inner conditional sections 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be ignored. The contents
of an ignored conditional section 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be parsed by ignoring all characters after
the "
html body div div div p code: [
html body div div div p: " following the keyword, except conditional section starts
"
html body div div div p code: <![
html body div div div p: " and ends "
html body div div div p code: ]]>
html body div div div p: ", until the matching conditional
section end is found. Parameter entity references 
html body div div div p em: MUST NOT
html body div div div p:  be recognized in this
process.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: If the keyword of the conditional section is a parameter-entity reference,
the parameter entity 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be replaced by its content before the processor
decides whether to include or ignore the conditional section.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: An example:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div pre: <!ENTITY % draft 'INCLUDE' >
<!ENTITY % final 'IGNORE' >
<![%draft;[
<!ELEMENT book (comments*, title, body, supplements?)>
]]>
<![%final;[
<!ELEMENT book (title, body, supplements?)>
]]>
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div:

html body div div h2: 
4 Physical Structures
html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : An XML document may consist of one
or many storage units. These
are called 
html body div div p b: entities
html body div div p: ; they all have 
html body div div p b: content
html body div div p:  and are
all (except for the 
html body div div p a: document entity
html body div div p:  and
the 
html body div div p a: external DTD subset
html body div div p: ) identified by
entity 
html body div div p b: name
html body div div p: .] Each XML document has one entity
called the 
html body div div p a: document entity
html body div div p: , which serves
as the starting point for the 
html body div div p a: XML processor
html body div div p: 
and may contain the whole document.
html body div div: 

html body div div p: Entities may be either parsed or unparsed. [
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : The contents of a 
html body div div p b: parsed
entity
html body div div p:  are referred to as its 
html body div div p a: replacement
text
html body div div p: ; this 
html body div div p a: text
html body div div p:  is considered an
integral part of the document.]

html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : An 
html body div div p b: unparsed entity
html body div div p: 
is a resource whose contents may or may not be 
html body div div p a: text
html body div div p: ,
and if text, may
be other than XML. Each unparsed entity has an associated 
html body div div p a: notation
html body div div p: , identified by name. Beyond a requirement
that an XML processor make the identifiers for the entity and notation available
to the application, XML places no constraints on the contents of unparsed
entities.]

html body div div: 

html body div div p: Parsed entities are invoked by name using entity references; unparsed entities
by name, given in the value of 
html body div div p b: ENTITY
html body div div p:  or 
html body div div p b: ENTITIES
html body div div p:  attributes.
html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : 

html body div div p b: General entities
html body div div p: 
are entities for use within the document content. In this specification, general
entities are sometimes referred to with the unqualified term 
html body div div p em: entity
html body div div p: 
when this leads to no ambiguity.]
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : 

html body div div p b: Parameter
entities
html body div div p:  are parsed entities for use within the DTD.]
These two types of entities use different forms of reference and are recognized
in different contexts. Furthermore, they occupy different namespaces; a parameter
entity and a general entity with the same name are two distinct entities.
html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h3: 

html body div div div h3:

html body div div div p: :  A 
html body div div div p b: character
reference
html body div div div p:  refers to a specific character in the ISO/IEC 10646 character
set, for example one not directly accessible from available input devices.]
