html body div div div div div p b: Validity constraint: Notation Declared
html body div div div div div p: 

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div div p: The 
html body div div div div div p a: Name
html body div div div div div p: 

html body div div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div div p:  match the declared name of a 
html body div div div div div p a: notation
html body div div div div div p: .

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 
						[
html body div div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div div p: : The 
html body div div div div p a: SystemLiteral
html body div div div div p:  is called the entity's 
html body div div div div p b: system
identifier
html body div div div div p: . It is meant to be
converted to a URI reference
(as defined in 
html body div div div div p a: [IETF RFC 3986]
html body div div div div p: ),
as part of the
process of dereferencing it to obtain input for the XML processor to construct the
entity's replacement text.] It is an error for a fragment identifier
(beginning with a 
html body div div div div p code: #
html body div div div div p:  character) to be part of a system identifier.
Unless otherwise provided by information outside the scope of this specification
(e.g. a special XML element type defined by a particular DTD, or a processing
instruction defined by a particular application specification), relative URIs
are relative to the location of the resource within which the entity declaration
occurs. This is defined to
be the external entity containing the '<' which starts the declaration, at the
point when it is parsed as a declaration.
A URI might thus be relative to the 
html body div div div div p a: document
entity
html body div div div div p: , to the entity containing the 
html body div div div div p a: external
DTD subset
html body div div div div p: , or to some other 
html body div div div div p a: external parameter
entity
html body div div div div p: . Attempts to
retrieve the resource identified by a URI 
html body div div div div p span: may
html body div div div div p:  be redirected at the parser
level (for example, in an entity resolver) or below (at the protocol level,
for example, via an HTTP 
html body div div div div p code: Location:
html body div div div div p:  header). In the absence of additional
information outside the scope of this specification within the resource,
the base URI of a resource is always the URI of the actual resource returned.
In other words, it is the URI of the resource retrieved after all redirection
has occurred.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: System
identifiers (and other XML strings meant to be used as URI references) 
html body div div div div p span: may
html body div div div div p:  contain
characters that, according to 
html body div div div div p a: [IETF RFC 3986]
html body div div div div p: ,
must be escaped before a URI can be used to retrieve the referenced resource. The
characters to be escaped are the control characters #x0 to #x1F and #x7F (most of
which cannot appear in XML), space #x20, the delimiters '<' #x3C, '>' #x3E and
'"' #x22, the 
html body div div div div p em: unwise
html body div div div div p:  characters '{' #x7B, '}' #x7D, '|' #x7C, '\' #x5C, '^' #x5E and
'`' #x60, as well as all characters above #x7F. Since escaping is not always a fully
reversible process, it 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  be performed only when absolutely necessary and as late
as possible in a processing chain. In particular, neither the process of converting
a relative URI to an absolute one nor the process of passing a URI reference to a
process or software component responsible for dereferencing it 
html body div div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div div p:  trigger escaping.
When escaping does occur, it 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  be performed as follows:
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div ol: 

html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol li p: Each character to be escaped is represented in
UTF-8 
html body div div div div ol li p a: [Unicode]
html body div div div div ol li p: 
as one or more bytes.
html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol: 

html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol li p: The resulting bytes are escaped with
the URI escaping mechanism (that is, converted to 
html body div div div div ol li p code: %
html body div div div div ol li p: 

html body div div div div ol li p var: HH
html body div div div div ol li p: ,
where HH is the hexadecimal notation of the byte value).
html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol: 

html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol li p: The original character is replaced by the resulting character sequence.
html body div div div div ol li: 

html body div div div div ol: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 
						[
html body div div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div div p: :  In addition to a system
identifier, an external identifier 
html body div div div div p span: may
html body div div div div p:  include a 
html body div div div div p b: public identifier
html body div div div div p: .]
An XML processor attempting to retrieve the entity's content 
html body div div div div p span: may
html body div div div div p:  use
any combination of
the public and system identifiers as well as additional information outside the
scope of this specification to try to generate an alternative URI reference.
If the processor is unable to do so, it 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  use the URI
reference specified in the system literal. Before a match is attempted,
all strings of white space in the public identifier 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  be normalized to
single space characters (#x20), and leading and trailing white space 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p: 
be removed.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Examples of external entity declarations:
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div div pre: <!ENTITY open-hatch
SYSTEM "http://www.textuality.com/boilerplate/OpenHatch.xml">
<!ENTITY open-hatch
PUBLIC "-//Textuality//TEXT Standard open-hatch boilerplate//EN"
"http://www.textuality.com/boilerplate/OpenHatch.xml">
<!ENTITY hatch-pic
SYSTEM "../grafix/OpenHatch.gif"
NDATA gif >

4.3.2 Well-Formed Parsed Entities
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: The document entity is well-formed if it matches the production labeled 
html body div div div div p a: document
html body div div div div p: . An external general parsed entity is well-formed
if it matches the production labeled 
html body div div div div p a: extParsedEnt
html body div div div div p: . All
external parameter entities are well-formed by definition.

html body div div div div div p:

html body div div div div p: A consequence of well-formedness in general

html body div div div div p: ,

reference
html body div div div div p: , or 
html body div div div div p a: entity reference
html body div div div div p: 
can begin in one entity and end in another.

4.3.3 Character Encoding in Entities
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Each external parsed entity in an XML document 
html body div div div div p span: may
html body div div div div p:  use a different encoding
for its characters. All XML processors 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  be able to read entities in both
the UTF-8 and UTF-16 encodings. The terms "UTF-8"
and "UTF-16" in this specification do not apply to character
encodings with any other labels, even if the encodings or labels are very
similar to UTF-8 or UTF-16.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Entities encoded in UTF-16 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  and entities
encoded in UTF-8 
html body div div div div p em: MAY
html body div div div div p:  begin with the Byte Order Mark described in
ISO/IEC 10646 
html body div div div div p a: [ISO/IEC 10646]
html body div div div div p:  or Unicode 
html body div div div div p a: [Unicode]
html body div div div div p: 
(the ZERO WIDTH NO-BREAK SPACE character, #xFEFF). This is an encoding signature,
not part of either the markup or the character data of the XML document. XML
processors 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  be able to use this character to differentiate between UTF-8
and UTF-16 encoded documents.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Although an XML processor is required to read only entities in the UTF-8
and UTF-16 encodings, it is recognized that other encodings are used around
the world, and it may be desired for XML processors to read entities that
use them. In
the absence of external character encoding information (such as MIME headers),
parsed entities which are stored in an encoding other than UTF-8 or UTF-16

html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  begin with a text declaration (see 
html body div div div div p a: 

html body div div div div p a b: 4.3.1 The Text Declaration
html body div div div div p a: 

html body div div div div p: ) containing
an encoding declaration:
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div h5: 

html body div div div div h5: 
Encoding Declaration
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div table: 

html body div div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 
[80]   
html body div div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td code: EncodingDecl
html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td:  ::=   
html body div div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td code: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td code a: S
html body div div div div table tbody tr td code:  'encoding' 
html body div div div div table tbody tr td code a: Eq
html body div div div div table tbody tr td code: 
('"'
html body div div div div table tbody tr td code a: EncName
html body div div div div table tbody tr td code:  '"' | "'"
html body div div div div table tbody tr td code a: EncName
html body div div div div table tbody tr td code: 
"'" ) 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div div table: 

html body div div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 
[81]   
html body div div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td code: EncName
html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td:  ::=   
html body div div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td code: [A-Za-z] ([A-Za-z0-9._] | '-')*
html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr td i: /* Encoding
name contains only Latin characters */
html body div div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div div table: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: In the 
html body div div div div p a: document entity
html body div div div div p: , the encoding
declaration is part of the 
html body div div div div p a: XML declaration
html body div div div div p: .
The 
html body div div div div p a: EncName
html body div div div div p:  is the name of the encoding used.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: In an encoding declaration, the values "
html body div div div div p code: UTF-8
html body div div div div p: ", "
html body div div div div p code: UTF-16
html body div div div div p: ",
"
html body div div div div p code: ISO-10646-UCS-2
html body div div div div p: ", and "
html body div div div div p code: ISO-10646-UCS-4
html body div div div div p: "

html body div div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div div p:  be used
for the various encodings and transformations of Unicode / ISO/IEC 10646,
the values "
html body div div div div p code: ISO-8859-1
html body div div div div p: ", "
html body div div div div p code: ISO-8859-2
html body div div div div p: ",
... "
html body div div div div p code: ISO-8859-
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p var: n
html body div div div div p: " (where 
html body div div div div p var: n
html body div div div div p: 
is the part number) 
html body div div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div div p:  be used for the parts of ISO 8859, and
the values "
html body div div div div p code: ISO-2022-JP
html body div div div div p: ", "
html body div div div div p code: Shift_JIS
html body div div div div p: ",
and "
html body div div div div p code: EUC-JP
html body div div div div p: "

html body div div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div div p:  be used for the various encoded
forms of JIS X-0208-1997. It
is 
html body div div div div p em: RECOMMENDED
html body div div div div p:  that character encodings registered (as 
html body div div div div p em: charset
html body div div div div p: s)
with the Internet Assigned Numbers Authority 
html body div div div div p a: [IANA-CHARSETS]
html body div div div div p: ,
other than those just listed, be referred to using their registered names;
other encodings 
html body div div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div div p:  use names starting with an "x-" prefix.
XML processors 
html body div div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div div p:  match character encoding names in a case-insensitive
way and 
html body div div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div div p:  either interpret an IANA-registered name as the encoding registered
at IANA for that name or treat it as unknown (processors are, of course, not
required to support all IANA-registered encodings).
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: In the absence of information provided by an external transport protocol
(e.g. HTTP or MIME), it is a 
html body div div div div p a: fatal error
html body div div div div p:  for
an entity including an encoding declaration to be presented to the XML processor
in an encoding other than that named in the declaration, or for an entity which
begins with neither a Byte Order Mark
nor an encoding declaration to use an encoding other than UTF-8. Note that
since ASCII is a subset of UTF-8, ordinary ASCII entities do not strictly
need an encoding declaration.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: It is a 
html body div div div div p a: fatal error
html body div div div div p:  for a 
html body div div div div p a: TextDecl
html body div div div div p:  to occur other
than at the beginning of an external entity.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: It is a 
html body div div div div p a: fatal error
html body div div div div p:  when an XML processor
encounters an entity with an encoding that it is unable to process. It
is a 
html body div div div div p a: fatal error
html body div div div div p:  if an XML entity is determined (via default, encoding declaration,
or higher-level protocol) to be in a certain encoding but contains byte
sequences that are not legal in that encoding. Specifically, it is a
fatal error if an entity encoded in UTF-8 contains any irregular code unit sequences,
as defined in Unicode 
html body div div div div p a: [Unicode]
html body div div div div p: . Unless an encoding
is determined by a higher-level protocol, it is also a 
html body div div div div p a: fatal error
html body div div div div p:  if an XML entity
contains no encoding declaration and its content is not legal UTF-8 or UTF-16.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Examples of text declarations containing encoding declarations:
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div div pre: <?xml encoding='UTF-8'?>
<?xml encoding='EUC-JP'?>

4.3.4 Version Information in Entities
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Each entity, including the 
html body div div div div p a: document entity
html body div div div div p: ,
can be separately
declared as XML 1.0 or XML 1.1. The version declaration appearing
in the document entity determines the version of the document as a
whole. An XML 1.1 document may invoke XML 1.0 external entities, so
that otherwise duplicated versions of external entities,
particularly DTD external subsets, need not be maintained. However,
in such a case the rules of XML 1.1 are applied to the entire
document.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p:  If an entity (including the document entity) is not labeled
with a version number, it is treated as if labeled as version
1.0.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h3: 

html body div div div h3: 
4.4 XML Processor Treatment of Entities and References
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The table below summarizes the contexts in which character references,
entity references, and invocations of unparsed entities might appear and the

html body div div div p em: REQUIRED
html body div div div p:  behavior of an 
html body div div div p a: XML processor
html body div div div p: 
in each case. The labels in the leftmost column describe the recognition context: 
html body div div div: 

html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dt: Reference in Content
html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dd: 

html body div div div dl dd p: as a reference anywhere after the 
html body div div div dl dd p a: start-tag
html body div div div dl dd p: 
and before the 
html body div div div dl dd p a: end-tag
html body div div div dl dd p:  of an element; corresponds
to the nonterminal 
html body div div div dl dd p a: content
html body div div div dl dd p: .

html body div div div dl dd: 

html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dt: Reference in Attribute Value
html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dd: 

html body div div div dl dd p: as a reference within either the value of an attribute in a 
html body div div div dl dd p a: start-tag
html body div div div dl dd p: ,
or a default value in an 
html body div div div dl dd p a: attribute declaration
html body div div div dl dd p: ;
corresponds to the nonterminal 
html body div div div dl dd p a: AttValue
html body div div div dl dd p: .

html body div div div dl dd: 

html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dt: Occurs as Attribute Value
html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dd: 

html body div div div dl dd p: as a 
html body div div div dl dd p a: Name
html body div div div dl dd p: , not a reference, appearing either as
the value of an attribute which has been declared as type 
html body div div div dl dd p b: ENTITY
html body div div div dl dd p: ,
or as one of the space-separated tokens in the value of an attribute which
has been declared as type 
html body div div div dl dd p b: ENTITIES
html body div div div dl dd p: .

html body div div div dl dd: 

html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dt: Reference in Entity Value
html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dd: 

html body div div div dl dd p: as a reference within a parameter or internal entity's 
html body div div div dl dd p a: literal
entity value
html body div div div dl dd p:  in the entity's declaration; corresponds to the nonterminal 
html body div div div dl dd p a: EntityValue
html body div div div dl dd p: .

html body div div div dl dd: 

html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dt: Reference in DTD
html body div div div dl: 

html body div div div dl dd: 

html body div div div dl dd p: as a reference within either the internal or external subsets of the 
html body div div div dl dd p a: DTD
html body div div div dl dd p: , but outside of an 
html body div div div dl dd p a: EntityValue
html body div div div dl dd p: ,
html body div div div dl dd p a: AttValue
html body div div div dl dd p: ,
html body div div div dl dd p a: PI
html body div div div dl dd p: ,
html body div div div dl dd p a: Comment
html body div div div dl dd p: ,
html body div div div dl dd p a: SystemLiteral

4.4.1 Not Recognized
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Outside the DTD, the 
html body div div div div p code: %
html body div div div div p:  character has no special significance;
thus, what would be parameter entity references in the DTD are not recognized
as markup in 
html body div div div div p a: content
html body div div div div p: . Similarly, the names of unparsed
entities are not recognized except when they appear in the value of an appropriately
declared attribute.

4.4.2 Included
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: 
						[
html body div div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div div p: : An entity is 
html body div div div div p b: included
html body div div div div p: 
when its 
html body div div div div p a: replacement text
html body div div div div p:  is retrieved
and processed, in place of the reference itself, as though it were part of
the document at the location the reference was recognized.] The replacement
text 
html body div div div div p span: may
html body div div div div p:  contain both 
html body div div div div p a: character data
html body div div div div p: 
and (except for parameter entities) 
html body div div div div p a: markup
html body div div div div p: ,
which 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  be recognized in the usual way. (The string "
html body div div div div p code: AT&amp;T;
html body div div div div p: "
expands to "
html body div div div div p code: AT&T;
html body div div div div p: " and the remaining ampersand
is not recognized as an entity-reference delimiter.) A character reference
is 
html body div div div div p b: included
html body div div div div p:  when the indicated character is processed in place
of the reference itself. 
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div h4: 

html body div div div div h4: 
4.4.3 Included If Validating
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: When an XML processor recognizes a reference to a parsed entity, in order
to 
html body div div div div p a: validate
html body div div div div p:  the document, the processor

html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p a: include
html body div div div div p:  its replacement text. If
the entity is external, and the processor is not attempting to validate the
XML document, the processor 
html body div div div div p em: MAY
html body div div div div p: , but need
not, include the entity's replacement text. If a non-validating processor
does not include the replacement text, it 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  inform the application that
it recognized, but did not read, the entity.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: This rule is based on the recognition that the automatic inclusion provided
by the SGML and XML entity mechanism, primarily designed to support modularity
in authoring, is not necessarily appropriate for other applications, in particular
document browsing. Browsers, for example, when encountering an external parsed
entity reference, might choose to provide a visual indication of the entity's
presence and retrieve it for display only on demand.

html body div div div div:

4.4.4 Forbidden
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: The following are forbidden, and constitute 
html body div div div div p a: fatal
errors
html body div div div div p: :

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div ul li p: the appearance of a reference to an 
html body div div div div ul li p a: unparsed
entity
html body div div div div ul li p: , except in the

html body div div div div ul li p a: EntityValue
html body div div div div ul li p:  in an entity declaration.
html body div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div ul li p: the appearance of any character or general-entity reference in the
DTD except within an 
html body div div div div ul li p a: EntityValue
html body div div div div ul li p:  or 
html body div div div div ul li p a: AttValue
html body div div div div ul li p: .

html body div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div ul: 

html body div div div div ul li: 

html body div div div div ul li p: a reference to an external entity in an attribute value.
html body div div div div ul li:

4.4.5 Included in Literal
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: When an 
html body div div div div p a: entity reference
html body div div div div p:  appears in
an attribute value, or a parameter entity reference appears in a literal entity
value, its 
html body div div div div p a: replacement text
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  be processed
in place of the reference itself as though it were part of the document at
the location the reference was recognized, except that a single or double
quote character in the replacement text 
html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  always be treated as a normal data
character and 
html body div div div div p em: MUST NOT
html body div div div div p:  terminate the literal. For example, this is well-formed:
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div div pre: <!ENTITY % YN '"Yes"' >
<!ENTITY WhatHeSaid "He said %YN;" >
html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: while this is not:
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div div pre: <!ENTITY EndAttr "27'" >
<element attribute='a-&EndAttr;>
html body div div div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div h4: 

html body div div div div h4:

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: When the name of an 
html body div div div div p a: unparsed entity
html body div div div div p: 
appears as a token in the value of an attribute of declared type 
html body div div div div p b: ENTITY
html body div div div div p: 
or 
html body div div div div p b: ENTITIES
html body div div div div p: , a validating processor

html body div div div div p a: system
html body div div div div p:  and 
html body div div div div p a: public

html body div div div div p:  be bypassed and left as is.

4.4.8 Included as PE
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: Just as with external parsed entities, parameter entities need only be 
html body div div div div p a: 

html body div div div div p a cite: included if validating
html body div div div div p a: 

html body div div div div p: . When a parameter-entity
reference is recognized in the DTD and included, its 
html body div div div div p a: replacement
text
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div div p:  be enlarged by the attachment of one leading and one following
space (#x20) character; the intent is to constrain the replacement text of
parameter entities to contain an integral number of grammatical tokens in
the DTD. This
behavior 
html body div div div div p em: MUST NOT
html body div div div div p:  apply to parameter entity references within entity values;
these are described in 
html body div div div div p a: 

html body div div div div p a b: 4.4.5 Included in Literal
html body div div div div p a: 

html body div div div div p: .

4.5 Construction of Entity Replacement Text
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: In discussing the treatment of entities, it is useful to distinguish
two forms of the entity's value.
[
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : For an
internal entity, the 
html body div div div p b: literal
entity value
html body div div div p:  is the quoted string actually present in the entity declaration,
corresponding to the non-terminal 
html body div div div p a: EntityValue
html body div div div p: .]
					[
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : For an external entity, the 
html body div div div p b: literal
entity value
html body div div div p:  is the exact text contained in the entity.]
					[
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : For an
internal entity, the 
html body div div div p b: replacement text
html body div div div p: 
is the content of the entity, after replacement of character references and
parameter-entity references.]
					[
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : For
an external entity, the 
html body div div div p b: replacement text
html body div div div p:  is the content of the entity,
after stripping the text declaration (leaving any surrounding white space) if there
is one but without any replacement of character references or parameter-entity
references.]

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The literal entity value as given in an internal entity declaration (
html body div div div p a: EntityValue
html body div div div p: )
html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  contain character, parameter-entity,
and general-entity references. Such references 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be contained entirely
within the literal entity value. The actual replacement text that is 
html body div div div p a: included
html body div div div p:  (or 
html body div div div p a: included in literal
html body div div div p: ) as described above

html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  contain the 
html body div div div p em: replacement
text
html body div div div p:  of any parameter entities referred to, and 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  contain the character
referred to, in place of any character references in the literal entity value;
however, general-entity references 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be left as-is, unexpanded. For example,
given the following declarations:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div pre: <!ENTITY % pub    "&#xc9;ditions Gallimard" >
<!ENTITY   rights "All rights reserved" >
<!ENTITY   book   "La Peste: Albert Camus,
&#xA9; 1947 %pub;. &rights;" >
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: then the replacement text for the entity "
html body div div div p code: book
html body div div div p: "
is:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div pre: La Peste: Albert Camus,
© 1947 Éditions Gallimard. &rights;
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The general-entity reference "
html body div div div p code: &rights;
html body div div div p: " would
be expanded should the reference "
html body div div div p code: &book;
html body div div div p: " appear
in the document's content or an attribute value.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: These simple rules may have complex interactions; for a detailed discussion
of a difficult example, see 
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p a b: C Expansion of Entity and Character References
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p: .

html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h3: 

html body div div div h3: 
4.6 Predefined Entities
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: 
					[
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : Entity and character references 
html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p: 
both be used to 
html body div div div p b: escape
html body div div div p:  the left angle bracket, ampersand, and
other delimiters. A set of general entities (
html body div div div p code: amp
html body div div div p: ,

html body div div div p code: lt
html body div div div p: ,

html body div div div p code: gt
html body div div div p: ,

html body div div div p code: apos
html body div div div p: ,

html body div div div p code: quot
html body div div div p: ) is specified for
this purpose. Numeric character references 
html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  also be used; they are expanded
immediately when recognized and 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be treated as character data, so the
numeric character references "
html body div div div p code: &#60;
html body div div div p: " and "
html body div div div p code: &#38;
html body div div div p: "
html body div div div p span: may
html body div div div p:  be used to escape 
html body div div div p code: <
html body div div div p:  and 
html body div div div p code: &
html body div div div p:  when they occur
in character data.]

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: All XML processors 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  recognize these entities whether they are declared
or not. 
html body div div div p a: For interoperability
html body div div div p: , valid XML
documents 
html body div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div p:  declare these entities, like any others, before using them. If
the entities 
html body div div div p code: lt
html body div div div p:  or 
html body div div div p code: amp
html body div div div p:  are declared, they 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be
declared as internal entities whose replacement text is a character reference
to the respective
character (less-than sign or ampersand) being escaped; the double
escaping is 
html body div div div p em: REQUIRED
html body div div div p:  for these entities so that references to them produce
a well-formed result. If the entities 
html body div div div p code: gt
html body div div div p: ,
html body div div div p code: apos
html body div div div p: ,
or 
html body div div div p code: quot
html body div div div p:  are declared, they 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be declared as internal entities
whose replacement text is the single character being escaped (or a character
reference to that character; the double escaping here is 
html body div div div p em: OPTIONAL
html body div div div p:  but harmless).
For example:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div pre: <!ENTITY lt     "&#38;#60;">
<!ENTITY gt     "&#62;">
<!ENTITY amp    "&#38;#38;">
<!ENTITY apos   "&#39;">
<!ENTITY quot   "&#34;">
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h3: 

html body div div div h3: 
4.7 Notation Declarations
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: 
					[
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : 

html body div div div p b: Notations
html body div div div p:  identify
by name the format of 
html body div div div p a: unparsed entities
html body div div div p: ,
the format of elements which bear a notation attribute, or the application
to which a 
html body div div div p a: processing instruction
html body div div div p:  is addressed.]

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: 
					[
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : 

html body div div div p b: Notation declarations
html body div div div p: 
provide a name for the notation, for use in entity and attribute-list declarations
and in attribute specifications, and an external identifier for the notation
which may allow an XML processor or its client application to locate a helper
application capable of processing data in the given notation.]

html body div div div h5:

html body div div div table tbody:

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p b: Validity constraint: Unique Notation Name
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div: 

html body div div div div p: A given 
html body div div div div p a: Name
html body div div div div p: 

html body div div div div p em: MUST NOT
html body div div div div p:  be declared in more than one notation declaration.
html body div div div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: XML processors 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  provide applications with the name and external identifier(s)
of any notation declared and referred to in an attribute value, attribute
definition, or entity declaration. They 
html body div div div p em: MAY
html body div div div p:  additionally resolve the external
identifier into the 
html body div div div p a: system identifier
html body div div div p: , file
name, or other information needed to allow the application to call a processor
for data in the notation described. (It is not an error, however, for XML
documents to declare and refer to notations for which notation-specific applications
are not available on the system where the XML processor or application is
running.)

4.8 Document Entity
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: 
					[
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : The 
html body div div div p b: document entity
html body div div div p: 
serves as the root of the entity tree and a starting-point for an 
html body div div div p a: XML processor
html body div div div p: .] This specification does
not specify how the document entity is to be located by an XML processor;
unlike other entities, the document entity has no name and might well appear
on a processor input stream without any identification at all.

5 Conformance
html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h3: 

html body div div div h3: 
5.1 Validating and Non-Validating Processors
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Conforming 
html body div div div p a: XML processors
html body div div div p:  fall into
two classes: validating and non-validating.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Validating and non-validating processors alike 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  report violations of
this specification's well-formedness constraints in the content of the 
html body div div div p a: document entity
html body div div div p:  and any other 
html body div div div p a: parsed
entities
html body div div div p:  that they read.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: 
					[
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: : 

html body div div div p b: Validating
processors
html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p: ,
at user option, report violations of the constraints expressed by
the declarations in the 
html body div div div p a: DTD
html body div div div p: , and failures
to fulfill the validity constraints given in this specification.]
To accomplish this, validating XML processors 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  read and process the entire
DTD and all external parsed entities referenced in the document.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Non-validating processors are 
html body div div div p em: REQUIRED
html body div div div p:  to check only the 
html body div div div p a: document
entity
html body div div div p: , including the entire internal DTD subset, for well-formedness. [
html body div div div p a: Definition
html body div div div p: :  While they are not required
to check the document for validity, they are 
html body div div div p em: REQUIRED
html body div div div p:  to 
html body div div div p b: process
html body div div div p: 
all the declarations they read in the internal DTD subset and in any parameter
entity that they read, up to the first reference to a parameter entity that
they do 
html body div div div p em: not
html body div div div p:  read; that is to say, they 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  use the information
in those declarations to 
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p a cite: normalize
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p: 
attribute values, 
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p a cite: include
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p:  the replacement
text of internal entities, and supply 
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p a cite: default
attribute values
html body div div div p a: 

html body div div div p: .] Except when 
html body div div div p code: standalone="yes"
html body div div div p: , they

html body div div div p em: MUST NOT
html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p a: process
html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p a: entity
declarations
html body div div div p:  or 
html body div div div p a: attribute-list declarations
html body div div div p: 
encountered after a reference to a parameter entity that is not read, since
the entity may have contained overriding declarations; when 
html body div div div p code: standalone="yes"
html body div div div p: , processors 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p: 
process these declarations.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Note
that when processing invalid documents with a non-validating
processor the application may not be presented with consistent
information.  For example, several requirements for uniqueness
within the document may not be met, including more than one element
with the same id, duplicate declarations of elements or notations
with the same name, etc.  In these cases the behavior of the parser
with respect to reporting such information to the application is
undefined.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: XML 1.1 processors 
html body div div div p em: MUST
html body div div div p:  be able to process both XML 1.0
and XML 1.1 documents.  Programs which generate XML 
html body div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div p: 
generate XML 1.0, unless one of the specific features of XML 1.1 is required.
html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h3: 

html body div div div h3: 
5.2 Using XML Processors
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: The behavior of a validating XML processor is highly predictable; it must
read every piece of a document and report all well-formedness and validity
violations. Less is required of a non-validating processor; it need not read
any part of the document other than the document entity. This has two effects
that may be important to users of XML processors:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div ul: 

html body div div div ul li: 

html body div div div ul li p: Certain well-formedness errors, specifically those that require reading
external entities, may fail to be detected by a non-validating processor. Examples
include the constraints entitled 
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p a cite: Entity Declared
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p: ,
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p a cite: Parsed Entity
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p: , and 
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p a cite: No
Recursion
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p: , as well as some of the cases described as 
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p a cite: forbidden
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p:  in 
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p a b: 4.4 XML Processor Treatment of Entities and References
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p: .

html body div div div ul li: 

html body div div div ul: 

html body div div div ul li: 

html body div div div ul li p: The information passed from the processor to the application may
vary, depending on whether the processor reads parameter and external entities.
For example, a non-validating processor may fail to 
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p a cite: normalize
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p: 
attribute values, 
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p a cite: include
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p:  the replacement
text of internal entities, or supply 
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p a cite: default
attribute values
html body div div div ul li p a: 

html body div div div ul li p: , where doing so depends on having read declarations
in external or parameter entities.
html body div div div ul li: 

html body div div div ul: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: For maximum reliability in interoperating between different XML processors,
applications which use non-validating processors 
html body div div div p em: SHOULD NOT
html body div div div p:  rely on any behaviors
not required of such processors.  Applications which require DTD facilities
not related to validation (such
as the declaration of default attributes and internal entities that are
or may be specified in
external entities
html body div div div p span: 
						)
html body div div div p: 

html body div div div p em: SHOULD
html body div div div p:  use validating XML processors.
html body div div div:

6 Notation
html body div div: 

html body div div p: The formal grammar of XML is given in this specification using a simple
Extended Backus-Naur Form (EBNF) notation. Each rule in the grammar defines
one symbol, in the form
html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div pre: symbol ::= expression
html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div p: Symbols are written with an initial capital letter if they are the
start symbol of a regular language, otherwise with an initial lowercase
letter. Literal strings are quoted.
html body div div: 

html body div div p: Within the expression on the right-hand side of a rule, the following expressions
are used to match strings of one or more characters: 
html body div div: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: #xN
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: where 
html body div div dl dd p code: N
html body div div dl dd p:  is a hexadecimal integer, the expression matches the character
whose number
(code point) in ISO/IEC 10646 is 
html body div div dl dd p code: N
html body div div dl dd p: . The number of leading zeros in the 
html body div div dl dd p code: #xN
html body div div dl dd p: 
form is insignificant.
html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: [a-zA-Z]
html body div div dl dt: ,
html body div div dl dt code: [#xN-#xN]
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: matches any 
html body div div dl dd p a: Char
html body div div dl dd p:  with a value in the range(s) indicated (inclusive).
html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: [abc]
html body div div dl dt: ,
html body div div dl dt code: [#xN#xN#xN]
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: matches any 
html body div div dl dd p a: Char
html body div div dl dd p:  with a value among the characters
enumerated. Enumerations and ranges can be mixed in one set of brackets.
html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: [^a-z]
html body div div dl dt: ,
html body div div dl dt code: [^#xN-#xN]
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: matches any 
html body div div dl dd p a: Char
html body div div dl dd p:  with a value 
html body div div dl dd p em: outside
html body div div dl dd p:  the range
indicated.
html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: [^abc]
html body div div dl dt: ,
html body div div dl dt code: [^#xN#xN#xN]
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: matches any 
html body div div dl dd p a: Char
html body div div dl dd p:  with a value not among the characters given. Enumerations
and ranges of forbidden values can be mixed in one set of brackets.
html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: "string"
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: matches a literal string 
html body div div dl dd p a: matching
html body div div dl dd p:  that
given inside the double quotes.
html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: 'string'
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: matches a literal string 
html body div div dl dd p a: matching
html body div div dl dd p:  that
given inside the single quotes.
html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div: 

html body div div p:  These symbols may be combined to match more complex patterns as follows,
where 
html body div div p code: A
html body div div p:  and 
html body div div p code: B
html body div div p:  represent simple expressions: 
html body div div: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: (
html body div div dl dt code: expression
html body div div dl dt: )

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: 

html body div div dl dd p code: expression
html body div div dl dd p:  is treated as a unit and may be combined as described
in this list.
html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: A?
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: matches 
html body div div dl dd p code: A
html body div div dl dd p:  or nothing; optional 
html body div div dl dd p code: A
html body div div dl dd p: .

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: A B
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: matches 
html body div div dl dd p code: A
html body div div dl dd p:  followed by 
html body div div dl dd p code: B
html body div div dl dd p: . This
operator has higher precedence than alternation; thus 
html body div div dl dd p code: A B | C D
html body div div dl dd p: 
is identical to 
html body div div dl dd p code: (A B) | (C D)
html body div div dl dd p: .

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: A | B
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: matches 
html body div div dl dd p code: A
html body div div dl dd p:  or 
html body div div dl dd p code: B
html body div div dl dd p: .

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: A - B
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: matches any string that matches 
html body div div dl dd p code: A
html body div div dl dd p:  but does not match 
html body div div dl dd p code: B
html body div div dl dd p: .

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: A+
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: matches one or more occurrences of 
html body div div dl dd p code: A
html body div div dl dd p: . Concatenation
has higher precedence than alternation; thus 
html body div div dl dd p code: A+ | B+
html body div div dl dd p:  is identical
to 
html body div div dl dd p code: (A+) | (B+)
html body div div dl dd p: .

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: A*
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: matches zero or more occurrences of 
html body div div dl dd p code: A
html body div div dl dd p: . Concatenation
has higher precedence than alternation; thus 
html body div div dl dd p code: A* | B*
html body div div dl dd p:  is identical
to 
html body div div dl dd p code: (A*) | (B*)
html body div div dl dd p: .

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div: 

html body div div p:  Other notations used in the productions are: 
html body div div: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: /* ... */
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: comment.
html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: [ wfc: ... ]
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: well-formedness constraint; this identifies by name a constraint on 
html body div div dl dd p a: well-formed
html body div div dl dd p:  documents associated with a production.
html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl dt code: [ vc: ... ]
html body div div dl dt: 

html body div div dl: 

html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl dd p: validity constraint; this identifies by name a constraint on 
html body div div dl dd p a: valid
html body div div dl dd p: 
documents associated with a production.
html body div div dl dd: 

html body div div dl:

B Definitions for Character Normalization
html body div div: 

html body div div p: This appendix contains the necessary definitions for character normalization.
For additional background information and examples, see 
html body div div p a: [Charmod]
html body div div p: .

html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : Text is said to be
in a 
html body div div p b: Unicode encoding form
html body div div p:  if it is encoded in
UTF-8, UTF-16 or UTF-32.]

html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : 

html body div div p b: Legacy encoding
html body div div p: 
is taken to mean any character encoding not based on Unicode.]

html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : A

html body div div p b: normalizing transcoder
html body div div p:  is a transcoder that converts from a

html body div div p a: legacy encoding
html body div div p:  to a

html body div div p a: Unicode encoding form
html body div div p:  and
ensures that the result is in Unicode Normalization Form C
(see UAX #15 
html body div div p a: [Unicode]
html body div div p: ).]

html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : A 
html body div div p b: character escape
html body div div p: 
is a syntactic device defined in a markup or programming language that allows
one or more of:]

html body div div: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol li p: expressing syntax-significant characters while disregarding
their significance in the syntax of the language, or
html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol li p: expressing characters not representable in the character encoding
chosen for an instance of the language, or
html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol li p: expressing characters in general, without use of the corresponding
character codes.
html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : 

html body div div p b: Certified
html body div div p:  text
is text which satisfies at least one of the following conditions:]

html body div div: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol li p: it has been confirmed through inspection that the text
is in normalized form
html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol li p: the source text-processing component is identified
and is known to produce only normalized text.
html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : Text is, for the purposes of
this specification, 
html body div div p b: Unicode-normalized
html body div div p:  if it is in a

html body div div p a: Unicode encoding form
html body div div p:  and is in
Unicode Normalization Form C, according to a version of Unicode Standard Annex #15:
Unicode Normalization Forms 
html body div div p a: [Unicode]
html body div div p:  at least as recent as the
oldest version of the Unicode Standard that contains all the characters
actually present in the text, but no earlier
than version 3.2.]

html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : Text is

html body div div p b: include-normalized
html body div div p:  if:]

html body div div: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol li p: the text is 
html body div div ol li p a: Unicode-normalized
html body div div ol li p: 
and does not contain any 
html body div div ol li p a: character escapes
html body div div ol li p: 
or 
html body div div ol li p a: includes
html body div div ol li p:  whose expansion would
cause the text to become no longer 
html body div div ol li p a: Unicode-normalized
html body div div ol li p: ;
or
html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol li p: the text is in a 
html body div div ol li p a: legacy encoding
html body div div ol li p:  and, if it were transcoded
to a 
html body div div ol li p a: Unicode encoding form
html body div div ol li p:  by a

html body div div ol li p a: normalizing transcoder
html body div div ol li p: , the resulting
text would satisfy clause 1 above.
html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : A 
html body div div p b: composing character
html body div div p: 
is a character that is one or both of the following:]

html body div div: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol li p: the second character in the canonical decomposition mapping of
some primary composite (as defined in D3 of UAX #15 
html body div div ol li p a: [Unicode]
html body div div ol li p: ), or
html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol li p: of non-zero canonical combining class (as defined in Unicode

html body div div ol li p a: [Unicode]
html body div div ol li p: ).

html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div: 

html body div div p: 
				
				[
html body div div p a: Definition
html body div div p: : Text is

html body div div p b: fully-normalized
html body div div p:  if:]

html body div div: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol li p: the text is in a 
html body div div ol li p a: Unicode encoding
form
html body div div ol li p: , is 
html body div div ol li p a: include-normalized
html body div div ol li p:  and
none of the 
html body div div ol li p a: relevant
constructs
html body div div ol li p:  comprising the text begin with a

html body div div ol li p a: composing character
html body div div ol li p:  or a
character escape representing a

html body div div ol li p a: composing character
html body div div ol li p: ; or
html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol: 

html body div div ol li: 

html body div div ol li p: the text is in a 
html body div div ol li p a: legacy encoding
html body div div ol li p:  and,
if it were transcoded to a 
html body div div ol li p a: Unicode encoding form
html body div div ol li p: 
by a 
html body div div ol li p a: normalizing transcoder
html body div div ol li p: , the resulting text
would satisfy clause 1 above.
html body div div ol li:

C Expansion of Entity and Character References (Non-Normative)
html body div div: 

html body div div p: This appendix contains some examples illustrating the sequence of entity-
and character-reference recognition and expansion, as specified in 
html body div div p a: 

html body div div p a b: 4.4 XML Processor Treatment of Entities and References
html body div div p a: 

html body div div p: .

html body div div: 

html body div div p: If the DTD contains the declaration
html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div pre: <!ENTITY example "<p>An ampersand (&#38;#38;) may be escaped
numerically (&#38;#38;#38;) or with a general entity
(&amp;amp;).</p>" >
html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div p: then the XML processor will recognize the character references when it
parses the entity declaration, and resolve them before storing the following
string as the value of the entity "
html body div div p code: example
html body div div p: ":

html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div pre: <p>An ampersand (&#38;) may be escaped
numerically (&#38;#38;) or with a general entity
(&amp;amp;).</p>
html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div p: A reference in the document to "
html body div div p code: &example;
html body div div p: "
will cause the text to be reparsed, at which time the start- and end-tags
of the 
html body div div p code: p
html body div div p:  element will be recognized and the three references will
be recognized and expanded, resulting in a 
html body div div p code: p
html body div div p:  element with the following
content (all data, no delimiters or markup):
html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div pre: An ampersand (&) may be escaped
numerically (&#38;) or with a general entity
(&amp;).
html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div p: A more complex example will illustrate the rules and their effects fully.
In the following example, the line numbers are solely for reference.
html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div pre: 1 <?xml version='1.
html body div div div pre span: 1
html body div div div pre: '?>
2 <!DOCTYPE test [
3 <!ELEMENT test (#PCDATA) >
4 <!ENTITY % xx '&#37;zz;'>
5 <!ENTITY % zz '&#60;!ENTITY tricky "error-prone" >' >
6 %xx;
7 ]>
8 <test>This sample shows a &tricky; method.</test>
html body div div div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div p: This produces the following:
html body div div: 

html body div div ul: 

html body div div ul li: 

html body div div ul li p: in line 4, the reference to character 37 is expanded immediately,
and the parameter entity "
html body div div ul li p code: xx
html body div div ul li p: " is stored in the symbol
table with the value "
html body div div ul li p code: %zz;
html body div div ul li p: ". Since the replacement
text is not rescanned, the reference to parameter entity "
html body div div ul li p code: zz
html body div div ul li p: "
is not recognized. (And it would be an error if it were, since "
html body div div ul li p code: zz
html body div div ul li p: "
is not yet declared.)
html body div div ul li: 

html body div div ul: 

html body div div ul li: 

html body div div ul li p: in line 5, the character reference "
html body div div ul li p code: &#60;
html body div div ul li p: "
is expanded immediately and the parameter entity "
html body div div ul li p code: zz
html body div div ul li p: "
is stored with the replacement text "
html body div div ul li p code: <!ENTITY tricky "error-prone">
html body div div ul li p: ", which is a well-formed entity declaration.
html body div div ul li: 

html body div div ul: 

html body div div ul li: 

html body div div ul li p: in line 6, the reference to "
html body div div ul li p code: xx
html body div div ul li p: " is recognized,
and the replacement text of "
html body div div ul li p code: xx
html body div div ul li p: " (namely "
html body div div ul li p code: %zz;
html body div div ul li p: ")
is parsed. The reference to "
html body div div ul li p code: zz
html body div div ul li p: " is recognized in
its turn, and its replacement text ("
html body div div ul li p code: <!ENTITY tricky "error-prone">
html body div div ul li p: ") is parsed. The general entity "
html body div div ul li p code: tricky
html body div div ul li p: "
has now been declared, with the replacement text "
html body div div ul li p code: error-prone
html body div div ul li p: ".

html body div div ul li: 

html body div div ul: 

html body div div ul li: 

html body div div ul li p: in line 8, the reference to the general entity "
html body div div ul li p code: tricky
html body div div ul li p: "
is recognized, and it is expanded, so the full content of the 
html body div div ul li p code: test
html body div div ul li p: 
element is the self-describing (and ungrammatical) string 
html body div div ul li p em: This sample
shows a error-prone method.
html body div div ul li p: 

html body div div ul li: 

html body div div ul: 

html body div div: 

html body div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div h2: 

html body div div h2: 
D Deterministic Content Models (Non-Normative)
html body div div: 

html body div div p: As
noted in 
html body div div p a: 

html body div div p a b: 3.2.1 Element Content
html body div div p a: 

html body div div p: , it is required that content
models in element type declarations be deterministic. This requirement is 
html body div div p a: for compatibility
html body div div p:  with SGML (which calls deterministic
content models "unambiguous"); XML processors built
using SGML systems may flag non-deterministic content models as errors.
html body div div: 

html body div div p: For example, the content model 
html body div div p code: ((b, c) | (b, d))
html body div div p:  is non-deterministic,
because given an initial 
html body div div p code: b
html body div div p:  the XML processor
cannot know which 
html body div div p code: b
html body div div p:  in the model is being matched without looking
ahead to see which element follows the 
html body div div p code: b
html body div div p: . In this case, the two references
to 
html body div div p code: b
html body div div p:  can be collapsed into a single reference, making the model read 
html body div div p code: (b,
(c | d))
html body div div p: . An initial 
html body div div p code: b
html body div div p:  now clearly matches only a single name
in the content model. The processor doesn't need to look ahead to see what follows; either 
html body div div p code: c
html body div div p:  or 
html body div div p code: d
html body div div p: 
would be accepted.
html body div div: 

html body div div p: More formally: a finite state automaton may be constructed from the content
model using the standard algorithms, e.g. algorithm 3.5 in section 3.9 of
Aho, Sethi, and Ullman 
html body div div p a: [Aho/Ullman]
html body div div p: . In many such algorithms, a follow
set is constructed for each position in the regular expression (i.e., each
leaf node in the syntax tree for the regular expression); if any position
has a follow set in which more than one following position is labeled with
the same element type name, then the content model is in error and may be
reported as an error.
html body div div: 

html body div div p: Algorithms exist which allow many but not all non-deterministic content
models to be reduced automatically to equivalent deterministic models; see
Brüggemann-Klein 1991 
html body div div p a: [Brüggemann-Klein]
html body div div p: .

html body div div: 

html body div: 

html body div div: 

html body div div h2: 

html body div div h2: 
E Autodetection of Character Encodings (Non-Normative)
html body div div: 

html body div div p: The XML encoding declaration functions as an internal label on each entity,
indicating which character encoding is in use. Before an XML processor can
read the internal label, however, it apparently has to know what character
encoding is in use — which is what the internal label is trying to indicate.
In the general case, this is a hopeless situation. It is not entirely hopeless
in XML, however, because XML limits the general case in two ways: each implementation
is assumed to support only a finite set of character encodings, and the XML
encoding declaration is restricted in position and content in order to make
it feasible to autodetect the character encoding in use in each entity in
normal cases. Also, in many cases other sources of information are available
in addition to the XML data stream itself. Two cases may be distinguished,
depending on whether the XML entity is presented to the processor without,
or with, any accompanying (external) information. We consider the first case
first.
html body div div: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div h3: 

html body div div div h3: 
E.1 Detection Without External Encoding Information
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Because each XML entity not accompanied by external
encoding information and not in UTF-8 or UTF-16 encoding must
begin with an XML encoding declaration, in which the first characters must
be '
html body div div div p code: <?xml
html body div div div p: ', any conforming processor can detect, after two
to four octets of input, which of the following cases apply. In reading this
list, it may help to know that in UCS-4, '<' is "
html body div div div p code: #x0000003C
html body div div div p: "
and '?' is "
html body div div div p code: #x0000003F
html body div div div p: ", and the Byte Order Mark
required of UTF-16 data streams is "
html body div div div p code: #xFEFF
html body div div div p: ". The notation

html body div div div p var: ##
html body div div div p:  is used to denote any byte value except that two consecutive

html body div div div p var: ##
html body div div div p: s cannot be both 00.
html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: With a Byte Order Mark:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div table: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: 00 00 FE
FF
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: UCS-4, big-endian machine (1234 order)
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: FF
FE 00 00
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: UCS-4, little-endian machine (4321 order)
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: 00 00 FF FE
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: UCS-4, unusual octet order (2143)
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: FE FF 00 00
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: UCS-4, unusual octet order (3412)
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: FE FF ## ##
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: UTF-16, big-endian
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: FF FE ## ##
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: UTF-16, little-endian
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: EF BB BF
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: UTF-8
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table: 

html body div div div: 

html body div div div p: Without a Byte Order Mark:
html body div div div: 

html body div div div table: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: 00 00 00 3C
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: UCS-4 or other encoding with a 32-bit code unit and ASCII
characters encoded as ASCII values, in respectively big-endian (1234), little-endian
(4321) and two unusual byte orders (2143 and 3412). The encoding declaration
must be read to determine which of UCS-4 or other supported 32-bit encodings
applies.

html body div div div table tbody tr td:

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody:

html body div div div table tbody tr td:

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: UTF-16BE or big-endian ISO-10646-UCS-2
or other encoding with a 16-bit code unit in big-endian order and ASCII characters
encoded as ASCII values (the encoding declaration must be read to determine
which)
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: 3C 00 3F 00
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: UTF-16LE or little-endian
ISO-10646-UCS-2 or other encoding with a 16-bit code unit in little-endian
order and ASCII characters encoded as ASCII values (the encoding declaration
must be read to determine which)
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: 3C 3F 78 6D
html body div div div table tbody tr td: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: UTF-8, ISO 646, ASCII, some part of ISO 8859, Shift-JIS, EUC, or any other
7-bit, 8-bit, or mixed-width encoding which ensures that the characters of
ASCII have their normal positions, width, and values; the actual encoding
declaration must be read to detect which of these applies, but since all of
these encodings use the same bit patterns for the relevant ASCII characters,
the encoding declaration itself may be read reliably

html body div div div table tbody tr td code: 4C
6F A7 94
html body div div div table tbody tr td:

html body div div div table tbody tr td: EBCDIC (in some flavor; the full encoding declaration
must be read to tell which code page is in use)
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody: 

html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: Other
html body div div div table tbody tr: 

html body div div div table tbody tr td: UTF-8 without an encoding declaration, or else the data stream is mislabeled
(lacking a required encoding declaration), corrupt, fragmentary, or enclosed
in a wrapper of some kind
